  1. I got this for my boyfriend for his birthday.   344. Reader, before my humble tale unfolds, you must know that I am not, nor have I ever been the most – how do I put this? – “manly” of young Englishmen. I was never one for sports in school, nor did I have the largest circle of school friends. I was, the wiry, knock-kneed kid with a bad haircut who could barely see without his glasses. Even in these later years, when adolescence and my university years have passed me by, I thought I was doomed to remain forever the weedy outcast, luckless with the ladies. Yes, friends, you may not think such a thing was possible now, but I had resigned myself to being just a humble, mild-mannered nerd who sought solace in his books and his few dear friends – but one fateful day, on a Wednesday around 4pm, in fact, all of that changed forever.<br /><br />I remembered that Internet favourite and former Star Trek alumni George Takei had released his own very pleasant-sounding fragrance on Amazon and I had a weekend with my friends planned in the trendy bars and clubs of London. I had been in the market for a new fragrance all week, to no avail. As my frustration grew, I took that fateful gamble on Takei’s foray into perfumery and ordered a bottle, from distant America. I thought that I had paid through the nose for shipping and packaging from so very far away, but I was wrong. Reader, let me assure you right away that no price on Earth could ever be too great for what was contained in that unassuming brown sleeve.<br /><br />It was a Saturday night, just around 6pm when everything changed. There I was, in my bathroom, in my best smart-casual efforts of a burgundy red dress shirt, jeans and smart shoes. Just my contact lenses now, and a spray of the bottle of Eau My stood on my counter, and I would be ready. Then it happened. Behind me, as the news droned on about some economic crisis or another in my living room, through some kind of osmosis or telepathy, the bottle of Eau My seemed to speak to me. Yes friends, like some ancient artefact of the gods themselves, that perfume that stood in its unassuming, quietly dignified way, like so many great men of the bridge on the Enterprise, reached out across the empty space between us and implored me to spray it before I did anything else. Not knowing what to expect, I extended a doubting hand towards the bottle, took it up towards my face and held it before me, looking at myself and the bottle in my mirror. Little could I have known that that was the last look I would ever take of myself as I was in those days. Before me, contained in that bottle was life, but not as I knew it. I took a deep breath, swallowed and let my finger press down on the button.<br /><br />At first, nothing happened. The perfume’s pleasant musk of ginger, jasmine and mandarin zest simply settled on my jaw and made its home on my cheekbones. I began to think it might only be a pleasant compliment to a good night out when all of a sudden, as I inhaled it deeply, something gave way deep inside of everything I was. Like something had hooked my insides with a coat hanger and violently jerked them back, I felt myself swaying and lurching and buckling under the weight of something awesomely powerful. Shocked as this force writhed and bucked and burrowed deep inside, I violently jerked a hand out towards my sink, desperate for something to grab on to, only for my toothbrush jar to come crashing down into pieces on my bathroom floor. Staggering in a daze to my bedroom, I collapsed into darkness on my bed. I don’t know what happened. I must have been out cold, but when I woke up, I felt somehow...different. A quick check of my wristwatch confirmed that this transformation had taken place inside of twenty minutes. So it was that I took several trepid, careful baby-steps back towards my bathroom, hoping to glimpse myself in my mirror and find some answers to what I had experienced.<br /><br />Reader, you would not believe what I saw staring back at me in that glass. Where there had once been nothing but the scrawny kid who never got picked for his games team, there now stood a captain’s physique. My shoulders, once bony and flat, were now as broad and as powerful as the stern of the Enterprise herself. My biceps bulged with the power to lift a man twice my size and as I looked at my rippling abdominal muscles, I thought that Thor himself could not have bested me if it ever came to a cheese-grating contest between us. As the shock lifted the fog of sleep from me, the notion that I might have accidentally fallen asleep with my contact lenses still on held no fear and gave way to joy, for I realised I no longer needed them because I could now see with flawless 20:20 vision. This, after a lifetime of crippling ocular disability, of short-sightedness and corrective glasses and prescription contact lenses. I was cured! Truly, I stood amazed – but the awesome power of Takei’s miracle Eau My was not spent yet. No, friends, far from it.<br /><br />Still reeling in amazement, I went to turn on the tap, hoping a splash of cold water would bring me to my senses. With nothing but a feather touch, the cold, hard steel was buckled and crushed into tangled remnants. There was no time to be bewildered though, because at that moment, the television I had so carelessly left on blared with urgent breaking news. Coming to, I dashed into my living room, whole chunks of plaster and wood splintering into dust as I rammed the doorframe by accident to see the story unfold. The news cameras reeled in horror and a million voices seemed to cry out in terror as high above my beloved London’s Leicester Square, a vast Klingon warship laid waste to my city with particle beam canon fire and artillery bombardment from their antimatter warheads. On the ground, the foot-soldiers were slaughtering innocents by their hundreds, and the Odeon Cinema was consumed by belching black smoke and fire and screams as they made war upon the Earth. No mere Amazon review could ever truly convey the horror of it to you, friends.<br /><br />It looked like my night out was cancelled. At least in the conventional sense, for what had once been only a frivolous online novelty purchase to go out and pick up girls (and possibly some young gentlemen...) on the town with suddenly became so much more as I realised what I now had to do with the incredible power of Eau My. With a mere thought, I was through my roof and into the cold night air, flying through the clouds faster than the warp drive output on Scotty’s best day. In an instant, as the invading Klingon warlord cried out in victory looking down upon his destruction, I came in for a spectacular, earth-shaking three-point landing in the middle of the square. So great was the quake of the earth when I touched down, that even under Klingon bombardment, it seemed like all of London stopped still to pay attention as I rose to my feet to face down the invasion. In those moments, I locked eyes with the warlord at the head of his fleet and my voice seemed to carry itself booming across the town.<br /><br />“Stop this at once!” I cried, “And leave this planet, or so help me, I’ll stop this myself!”<br /><br />A moment of silence passed, as though tumbleweed might have blown by if this were the American Wild West, before the entire invasion fleet seemed to burst into peels of guttural laughter at my threats. In moments, though, the humour of my feeble protestations faded into over-boiling primal rage that I would dare to impugn their warriors’ honour, and as if to prove their point, I was charged by several of the villains, who came at my with their spears and rifles like a swarm of enraged – although mildly entertained – hornets.<br /><br />As they charged, either from some lost oblivion deep within my psyche, or else stirred into waking life by the power of Eau My, was the sudden absolute mastery of all forms of moQbara combat. I met the first blow with an almost casual resistance, holding out my left forearm and planting my feet as the sharp steel of a bat’leth tore through my shirt and gnawed at my arm. I met the Klingon’s attack with a return right hook to his jaw so powerful that it sent the villain flying three feet across the ground and tore him from his weapon, still embedded in my arm.<br /><br />Pulling the blade from my flesh, I was amazed to discover that the wound stitched itself back together without even the trace of a scar before my very eyes, when I primed the bat’leth for combat, holding it steady and standing ready in the middle of the invasion, daring any of the warriors to face me in honourable mano-a-mano fisticuffs. With their strict warrior code demanding they face me one-by-one, what followed was a violent ballet of vicious alien king-fu. As the hours wore on, the odds mounted so high against their forces – almost as high as I would leap into the air, dragging my Klingon opponent up with me in anticipation of a truly epic clothesline body-slam - that some even dared to fire on me from the sidelines with their anti-matter rifles.<br /><br /> It was at these moments that I stood in awe of myself as I realised what I been transformed into - I may have been wearing a red shirt, but the molecules of Takei’s perfume were somehow able to rearrange themselves in an instant, forming some kind of chemical cologne barrier around me powerful enough to repel Klingon weapon fire. The most savage heat-ray blasts at almost point-blank range bounced off of me like phaser fire from the Enterprise’s forward shields. It was all I could do to invite these code-disgracing felons to fight me one-to-one with whatever shred of dignity they had left, to spare them the humiliation of ritual suicide or execution.<br /><br /> By the end of the night, I had laid waste to the entire Klingon invasion force single-handed, with bodies lying dead or out cold or exhausted all around me. Only the would-be warlord of these alien usurpers of my planetremained, who leapt down from his command post, alive with the all the impotent rage of his fallen army into an earth-shaking three-point landing of his own, charging at me at full speed, the tip of his bat’leth primed to run my right through. Ducking and dodging, and getting up to face him for another round, he roared a terrible, primal raw, charging me again – but this time, I was ready.<br />Even as he put all of his mastery of the bat’leth against me, I blocked and dodged with the skill of the old Klingon masters, narrowly avoiding a sweeping arc through the air that would have taken off my head. As he was thrown off balance by the force of his swing, I mule-kicked him from a hand-stand position, sending him stumbling back, his weapon falling from his hand.<br /><br />Leaping back onto my feet, I ran him down, so that even as he stood legs apart ready to tackle me like a man stopping a charging bull with his bare hands, I threw myself down into a body-slide between his legs – and in those moments, I got right up, brought him around to face my by his shoulder and punched him in the face. A few moments of stunned disbelief passed in his face, which steadily bruised before he collapsed, first onto his knees, then out cold, face down onto the tarmac of Leicester Square.<br /><br />All around me, London seemed to erupt into cheers and adulation. Every news camera, helicopter and reporter for miles went ballistic with coverage of what had happened. The Mayor of London himself even ran up to me with the Prime Minister and both of them tried to pin every medal awarded in the British Army to my chest in a fit of grateful hysteria Rock-solid marriages of fifteen or more years and long partnerships were abandoned on the spot. Wives, husbands, boyfriends and girlfriends, girlfriends of girlfriends (oh my!) and boyfriends of boyfriends all dropped to their knees with desperate tears in their eyes like a reverse Mexican wave of lovesick agony, begging and pleading for my hand in marriage – but it was in those moments that I realised for certain what Eau My had turned me into – what I had become, and what I would be forever. Turning down medals and marriages and the media frenzy, and politely informing a panicked chap in a bow-tie who emerged from a blue box from 1963 that the crisis had been averted, I turned my back on the city and took off into the night air again. “I must go now,” I said to them, “but remember – it’s ok to be Takei.”<br /><br />I live my life in the same quiet solitude in which it began, but now I do it as a different man. Wherever there is a threat from the stars emerging to attack the Earth, I will be there to defend it, and at my side will be that bottle of Eau My that changed my life forever. People of the Earth, I am not telling you to not buy this truly amazing product of perfumery. I am simply urging caution – for as everyone knows, with great power must come great responsibility and it must only be used it you are willing to boldly go where no man has gone before.
